January 26: (TW: flashing lights) President Clinton holds a press conference focusing on education, and at the end of his address, denies the affair with intern Monica Lewinsky. Here's his statement:
"Now I have to go back to work on my State of the Union speech...but I want to say one thing to the American people. I want you to listen to me, I'm going to say this again: I did not have sexual relations with that woman, Miss Lewinsky. I never told anybody to lie, not a single time, never. These allegations are false, and I need to go back to work for the American people. Thank you."

(article only) April 1: Nunavut becomes officially separated from the Northwestern Territories in Canada, and Paul Okalik is sworn in as its first premier. April 1: Isard's Revenge, the eighth novel in the Star Wars: X-Wing series, is published. April 1: Square releases SaGa Frontier 2 (article here) for the PlayStation in Japan. April 1: The National Minimum Wage Act 1998 takes effect, where the minimum wage in the UK is set to £3.60 an hour for workers over the age of 21, and £3 an hour for workers under 21. The wage rates are adjusted every October (until this year and 2016, which now adjusts the rates every April and October) and eventually expanded to include apprentices, workers around the ages of 16-17, and to 21-24 year olds.
